  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_97f8b07c-ec17-4950-ab83-e0fb6551f70a'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer8274324282219372565">In this groundbreaking, painted graphic novel, the inmates of Arkham Asylum have taken over Gotham's detention center for the criminally insane on April Fools' Day, demanding Batman in exchange for their hostages. Accepting their demented challenge, Batman is forced to live and endure the personal hells of the Joker, Scarecrow, Poison Ivy, Two-Face, and many other sworn en</span>
  <span id="freeText8274324282219372565" style="display:none">In this groundbreaking, painted graphic novel, the inmates of Arkham Asylum have taken over Gotham's detention center for the criminally insane on April Fools' Day, demanding Batman in exchange for their hostages. Accepting their demented challenge, Batman is forced to live and endure the personal hells of the Joker, Scarecrow, Poison Ivy, Two-Face, and many other sworn enemies in order to save the innocents and retake the prison. During his run through this absurd gauntlet, the Dark Knight's own sanity is placed in jeopardy. This special anniversary edition trade paperback also reproduces the original script with annotations by Morrison and editor Karen Berger.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8274324282219372565" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17129709662663648685">The Caped Crusader with footnotes!?!<br/><br/>or Art for Art’s Sake.<br/><br/>or Holy Histrionics, Batman, I’d rather have listened to an opera…<br/><br/>Grant Morrison gets “serious” – it’s even mentioned in the title twice in case you need a reminder – and if Carrot Top wants to star in a remake of Death of a Salesman or Billy Joel wants to write a concerto for flugelhorn and triangle, I don’t want to hear about it.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449843545i/17347308._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>Wait, Jeff, did you say footnotes?</i><br/><br/>Yes, Goodreader, this is why I love you, because nothing ever gets by you. </span>
  <span id="freeText17129709662663648685" style="display:none">The Caped Crusader with footnotes!?!<br><br>or Art for Art’s Sake.<br><br>or Holy Histrionics, Batman, I’d rather have listened to an opera…<br><br>Grant Morrison gets “serious” – it’s even mentioned in the title twice in case you need a reminder – and if Carrot Top wants to star in a remake of Death of a Salesman or Billy Joel wants to write a concerto for flugelhorn and triangle, I don’t want to hear about it.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449843545i/17347308._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Wait, Jeff, did you say footnotes?</i><br><br>Yes, Goodreader, this is why I love you, because nothing ever gets by you. Nothing.<br><br>This is the 25th anniversary edition of the publishing of this pretentious pile of crap, so we get Morrison’s script tacked onto the actual comic. The script includes footnotes because Mr. Morrison wants to share each and every pop culture allusion and Easter egg that he’s cleverly included for us.<br><br>The script actually came in handy, because I could actually read what The Joker was trying to say, but shuffling back and forth between the comic and an addendum quickly wore thin.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449843545i/17347310._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A plot summary: The inmates at Arkham take control of the asylum because it’s Tuesday and demand that Batman pay them a visit, because they love him so so much and want to cuddle and spoon and eat Toll House cookie dough real fast, which is a good thing because this isn’t take-control-of-the-situation-with-a-few-well-placed-bat-flash-gernades-and-a-couple-of-kidney-punches-and-or-batarang-or-two-to-the-dome Batman, this is Emo-boy-Mr.-Feels-Kyle-Raynor-is-my-psychic-twin Batman, so let’s brood, shall we?<br><br>Therapy seems to work wonders for a few of the rogues – yes, Two-Face <s>flip a coin</s> pick a card to see if you can scratch your ass.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449843853i/17347362.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The rest:<br><br>Mad Hatter:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449843545i/17347311.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Stop spouting drivel and take a tranquilizer!<br><br>Clayface:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449843545i/17347312.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>He’s seen better days. <br><br>Idea: Bats, shove him into a kiln and present him to Alfred as a big ashtray or something. You can put him between the dinosaur and the big penny.<br><br>Did I mention that the asylum is haunted because the Arkham’s were a bunch of loons or the Arkham’s were a bunch of loons <i> because </i> the original house was haunted?<br><br>No? Sorry.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449843545i/17347313._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br><b>Bottom line</b>: The art is purty, but then so was Where’s Waldo? And with Where’s Waldo you didn’t have to work as hard to find the player(s).<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449843545i/17347314._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Another word association? Ready?<br><br>This book…………………….Crap.</span>

<div id="review_338088279" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/338088279" />
    <a title="Eric" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/76688-eric"><img alt="Eric" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1255373698p2/76688.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/338088279?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eric" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eric" href="/user/show/76688-eric">Eric</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">No one</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76688-eric?shelf=batman">batman</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76688-eric?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer338088279" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1185635069670281636">What a fucking mess. The painted artwork was appalling, the story-line was incoherent, the dialogue was barely legible, and, most importantly, the portrayal of Batman was all wrong. This felt like a second-rate haunted-house horror that Batman was wedged into, and poorly at that. Batman's encounters with various villains felt thrown-in, in a cheap name-dropping way, his decision-making was baffling to non-existent, and the story's resolution -- hanging on a coin-flip -- was absurd. <br/><br/>The back-stor</span>
  <span id="freeText1185635069670281636" style="display:none">What a fucking mess. The painted artwork was appalling, the story-line was incoherent, the dialogue was barely legible, and, most importantly, the portrayal of Batman was all wrong. This felt like a second-rate haunted-house horror that Batman was wedged into, and poorly at that. Batman's encounters with various villains felt thrown-in, in a cheap name-dropping way, his decision-making was baffling to non-existent, and the story's resolution -- hanging on a coin-flip -- was absurd. <br /><br />The back-story to Gotham's Arkham Asylum was done much better in the Batman: Arkham Asylum video-game. If I'd read this first, I may never have played that game due to fear it was this bad. <br /><br />I only did decide to read this after seeing it on <a href="http://forbiddenplanet.com/picks/50-best-graphic-novels/" rel="nofollow noopener">multiple</a> <a href="http://bookstove.com/book-talk/10-graphic-novels-every-fan-of-literature-should-read/" rel="nofollow noopener">best</a> <a href="http://blog.flipkart.com/top-ten-greatest-batman-graphic-novels-frank-miller-jeph-loeb-alan-moore" rel="nofollow noopener">graphic-novel</a> <a href="http://estranged911.hubpages.com/hub/Top-graphic-novels" rel="nofollow noopener">lists</a>. How can so many lists be so wrong? And how is the Goodreads rating so high? What am I missing?</span>
  <a data-text-id="1185635069670281636" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_170871002" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/170871002" />
    <a title="Keith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31002-keith"><img alt="Keith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471996653p2/31002.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/170871002?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keith" href="/user/show/31002-keith">Keith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31002-keith?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer170871002" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8613414606882966398">So after buying this book for the third time in my life today (the first, a hardcover edition that all the pages eventually fell out of; the second, the paperback edition sans script that now sits across the country with the rest of my books) I decided it was worth going on Goodreads to wax poetic about it. Because goddamn I love this book. I got it right after the '89 movie came out, of course, and was absolutely terrified of it -- it sat on my nightstand and gave me nightmares regularly, until</span>
  <span id="freeText8613414606882966398" style="display:none">So after buying this book for the third time in my life today (the first, a hardcover edition that all the pages eventually fell out of; the second, the paperback edition sans script that now sits across the country with the rest of my books) I decided it was worth going on Goodreads to wax poetic about it. Because goddamn I love this book. I got it right after the '89 movie came out, of course, and was absolutely terrified of it -- it sat on my nightstand and gave me nightmares regularly, until I put it away for years before revisiting it again in my late teens.<br /><br />But I'd never bothered to wonder what anyone else thought of it. It's so weird and relatively incomprehensible that I wouldn't recommend it to people trying to get into comics, and most people who are into comics have already read it, I imagine (despite, as I said, never having talked about it with anyone). <br /><br />So yeah! Goodreads! Goodreads kinda hates this book! I mean, not everybody, but a lot of people! And Batman comics are not the kind of thing that generally creates polarized opinions, if ya know what I mean. There's The Bat-Books Fans Like and The Bat-Books Fans Hate, and every so often there's some idiot who goes "I just think Alan Moore over-intellectualizes" and we all beat up that one guy. And sure, everyone argues if <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/96358.Batman_The_Killing_Joke" title="Batman The Killing Joke by Alan Moore" rel="nofollow noopener">Killing Joke</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/59980.Batman_Year_One" title="Batman Year One by Frank Miller" rel="nofollow noopener">Year One</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/59960.Batman_The_Dark_Knight_Returns" title="Batman The Dark Knight Returns by Frank Miller" rel="nofollow noopener">Dark Knight Returns</a> is the best one, but it's generally assumed that ONE of them is your favorite (and then a couple n00bs in the back start saying that either <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6375845.Batman_Hush" title="Batman Hush by Jeph Loeb" rel="nofollow noopener">Hush</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/106069.Batman_The_Long_Halloween" title="Batman The Long Halloween by Jeph Loeb" rel="nofollow noopener">Long Halloween</a> is the best, and we throw them out with the Alan Moore whiny guy). But <i>Arkham Asylum</i>? I dunno man. It's a weird friggin' book. It's apparently like the best-selling graphic novel of all time. It rarely comes up in discussion. And Goodreads kinda hates it.<br /><br />Everyone who complains that Grant Morrison's cleverer-than-thou new age fruitiness is too naked here is right. And that Dave McKean clearly rendered Batman as a black splotch because he couldn't figure out how to draw him, that's also obvious. And that Batman acts completely out-of-character -- he doesn't save anyone, he lets people kill each other, he has no discernible plan, he admits he's just scared and then leaves at the end -- yeah, those folks are right too.<br /><br />But dammit. People like Batman because we all kind feel like we ARE Batman, I think. Not like we have hero complexes - but like we're alone on the edge of an abyss, either the sanest or the least sane in a strange dark world? You don't have to be thirteen in your bedroom listening to the Cure to grok that, man. And yknow, I'm glad there's a fucked-up scary Bat-book where Batman is just doing all he can to stand upright in the face of muddy horror, you know? With its facile Crowley references and lame-ass anglocentric Tarot-based page layouts or whatever. Cuz good lord, some days your whole world feels like an ominous Tarot reading, no matter how far you get from that little kid who was scared of his own comics twenty years ago. I'm glad there's a book out there where my buddy Batman has a bad day too.<br /><br />Loves you, booky-book. Loves you. No matter what the little piggies say.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8613414606882966398" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_237208891" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/237208891" />
    <a title="Shannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6773727-shannon"><img alt="Shannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579036502p2/6773727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/237208891?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon" href="/user/show/6773727-shannon">Shannon</a>

        rated it

There's a two part story here where we switch back and forth to the founder of Arkham and why he turned his mansion into a facility for the mad and Batman trying to navigate his way through the madness of Arkham. <br/><br/><a href='http://imgur.com/4c5dXaW' title='' rel='nofollow noopener'>

There's a two part story here where we switch back and forth to the founder of Arkham and why he turned his mansion into a facility for the mad and Batman trying to navigate his way through the madness of Arkham. <br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/4c5dXaW" title="" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>Batman action is minimal. This is much more of an emotional journey. <br><br>There is distinctive lettering for different characters and massive amounts of symbolism so several things will be missed by the casual reader. Think of this as a true nightmare tale for Batman. Sometimes the symbolism is a bit much and gets in the way of the tale. This graphic novel influenced a video game of a similar title but that one is more action based. It also influenced Heath Ledger's portrayal of The Joker. <br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/1DRwrmY" title="" rel="nofollow noopener">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_223941104" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/223941104" />
    <a title="Sam Quixote" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote"><img alt="Sam Quixote" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529183438p2/5759543.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/223941104?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam Quixote" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam Quixote" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote">Sam Quixote</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer223941104" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11194345953184783838">Based solely upon his 2006-2013 run, Grant Morrison might be the greatest Batman writer of all time. But he wasn’t always so brilliant as his first Batman book, the mega-selling Arkham Asylum: A Serious House on Serious Earth, shows. <br/><br/>The inmates have overrun the asylum and are holding civilians hostage. With Joker running free with a knife, Batman goes into the asylum to stop him and enters a nightmarish netherworld. Meanwhile, the troubled life of the asylum’s founder, Amadeus Arkham, is explor</span>
  <span id="freeText11194345953184783838" style="display:none">Based solely upon his 2006-2013 run, Grant Morrison might be the greatest Batman writer of all time. But he wasn’t always so brilliant as his first Batman book, the mega-selling Arkham Asylum: A Serious House on Serious Earth, shows. <br /><br />The inmates have overrun the asylum and are holding civilians hostage. With Joker running free with a knife, Batman goes into the asylum to stop him and enters a nightmarish netherworld. Meanwhile, the troubled life of the asylum’s founder, Amadeus Arkham, is explored. <br /><br />The story is one long rambling mess, which is part of Morrison’s intent. It’s designed to be dream-like and to read like a song and therefore, as a comic, it’s difficult to follow or really understand. I get the impression the symbolism of the tarot is important but the book didn’t make me interested enough to want to pursue a deeper understanding of it. Batman’s characterisation is a bit off too – how was he beaten by a deranged doctor!? <br /><br />Some readers might scoff that Morrison’s comics are always like this with his drug use, but he actually wrote this before he began using drugs and alcohol – he writes in his afterword that he stayed up for hours on end to achieve the altered state of consciousness he wanted before sitting down to write. So it’s official: with or without drugs, Morrison writes weird comics! Hear that, poseur artists, you don’t need vice to produce art! <br /><br />Dave McKean’s artwork matches Morrison’s bizarre story well but it still looks a bit too avant-garde for a comic. McKean’s best known for being The Sandman’s cover artist and his art is well suited to that format. But for page after page of interior art? It’s just headache-inducing! And when he does draw distinguishable figures, they look like poor Simon Bisley facsimiles. <br /><br />I liked Morrison’s idea to have the Arkham doctors try weaning Harvey Dent off of the two-sided coin and onto the I Ching. It seemed like an original and viable means of treatment for Two-Face. But other ideas like the Joker calling the outside world the asylum and the world inside Arkham the real world was just corny, and the Amadeus Arkham storyline just read like a poor man’s Psycho. Morrison’s comics usually have more substance to them but Arkham Asylum is all surface texture with few great ideas. <br /><br />Arkham Asylum is a visually interesting book but it looks and reads like an art student’s project, ie. a pretentious mish-mash of nonsense, than a good comic. I definitely wouldn’t rank it among Batman’s classics! If you want to read Morrison’s best Batman books, start with Batman and Son and go forwards from there. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11194345953184783838" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_27269308" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/27269308" />
    <a title="Andrew Webb" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1244994-andrew-webb"><img alt="Andrew Webb" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/27269308?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew Webb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew Webb" href="/user/show/1244994-andrew-webb">Andrew Webb</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" 9783866070868" href="/book/show/2899894-batman">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer27269308" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11285289359511017043">I have read many a poor/overrated Batman story in my ten-odd years as a fan, but this much referred to epic may take the cake. As a Batman story, this is a total failure. Batman acts completely out of character almost from the beginning. When walking into a hostage situation masterminded by the Joker, he strikes up a conversation with his archenemy rather than planning how to rescue the innocents involved. When Joker shoots a hostage in the head across the room from Batman (I think-- the bizarre</span>
  <span id="freeText11285289359511017043" style="display:none">I have read many a poor/overrated Batman story in my ten-odd years as a fan, but this much referred to epic may take the cake. As a Batman story, this is a total failure. Batman acts completely out of character almost from the beginning. When walking into a hostage situation masterminded by the Joker, he strikes up a conversation with his archenemy rather than planning how to rescue the innocents involved. When Joker shoots a hostage in the head across the room from Batman (I think-- the bizarre art style makes it nearly impossible to tell what is occuring at times), Batman makes no attempt to save the hostage or capture the Joker.<br /><br />In fact, the story seems to be more allegorical than literal, by showing Batman conversing with many of his rogues gallery foes rather than fighting them. But rather than a meaningful point, the book seems to meander until it becomes a random melange of images with little relation to one another. Batman accomplishes next to nothing by the end of the story, with little explanation as to why. It is as though he started a mission, then thought better of it and decided to take a walk through Gotham Park instead.<br /><br />In the end, this book is somewhat reminiscent of the film "Batman Returns"-- truly bizarre, with a completely different "Batman" than whatever iconic version lodges in the minds of his fans (the early comics, the campy 60s TV show, the 90s animated series, etc.). However, while Batman Returns is original enough to watch for mere discussions' sake, and at least offers a story of Batman fighting to protect Gotham citizens, this unfortunate graphic novel is worth reading only for the most completive Batman fan.<br /><br />This book is, in short, postmodern garbage.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11285289359511017043" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_7763801" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/7763801" />
    <a title="Marc" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/173475-marc"><img alt="Marc" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/7763801?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marc" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marc" href="/user/show/173475-marc">Marc</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">intellectual art lovers</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer7763801" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5298962560578279455">Arkham Asylum is the best graphic novel I've ever read for two reasons: writing, and art.<br/><br/>This isn't your average WHACK! POW! comic book. In fact, there is almost no violence or glammed-out secret weapons. Grant Morrision takes us through a masterful exploration into the psyche of Bruce Wayne, a man who suffered a tragic loss at an early age and formed a very clear alternate identity. Is he a crime fighter, or does he suffer from MPD (Multiple Personality Disorder), and does it even matter.<br/><br/>Set in</span>
  <span id="freeText5298962560578279455" style="display:none">Arkham Asylum is the best graphic novel I've ever read for two reasons: writing, and art.<br /><br />This isn't your average WHACK! POW! comic book. In fact, there is almost no violence or glammed-out secret weapons. Grant Morrision takes us through a masterful exploration into the psyche of Bruce Wayne, a man who suffered a tragic loss at an early age and formed a very clear alternate identity. Is he a crime fighter, or does he suffer from MPD (Multiple Personality Disorder), and does it even matter.<br /><br />Set in the halls of Arkham Aslyum, home to "inmates" like the Joker and the original MPD superstar, Harvey "Two Face" Dent, this tale is creepy as you begin to realize that this particular fight will not be done with fists and bat belts.<br /><br />The only thing that tops the writing is the art. Dave McKean uses traditional and digital media to create a world that feels as crazy as it's written to be. The echos in Batman's head are shown in a fashion that you can almost taste and smell. I found myself saying, "yes, that's what that thought or feeling must LOOK like."<br /><br />No other graphic novel has ever matched art and writing so perfectly. If you read one graphic novel in your life, and if you want to see that even the most pop-star of comic heroes can be gritty and real, read this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5298962560578279455" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3363390020" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14361344150206234257">"Until the night of 1901, when I first caught a glimpse of that other world. The world of the dark side."<br/><br/>From these lines on the first page, I knew this was going to be a dark ride. The artwork from the inside front-cover to the inside back-cover helped maintain continuity of oppressive psychological heaviness. It was fun to read and look at the unique artwork because of the various references and symbolisms. <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1591581795i/29611737._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>I enjoyed this one from start to finish. The inmates of the infamous Arkham Asylum have</span>
  <span id="freeText14361344150206234257" style="display:none">"Until the night of 1901, when I first caught a glimpse of that other world. The world of the dark side."<br><br>From these lines on the first page, I knew this was going to be a dark ride. The artwork from the inside front-cover to the inside back-cover helped maintain continuity of oppressive psychological heaviness. It was fun to read and look at the unique artwork because of the various references and symbolisms. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1591581795i/29611737._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I enjoyed this one from start to finish. The inmates of the infamous Arkham Asylum have rioted and taken over. The Joker and the other criminals demand Batman make a personal appearance inside the asylum. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1591581795i/29611738._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>He is forced to enter the asylum where he undergoes his own dark psychological journey while dealing with a few villains. While Batman briefly encounters Two-Face, Mad Hatter, Killer Croc, Scarecrow, and others, the plot tells the backstory of the asylum's dark beginning.<br><br>The parallel story within the plot is about Dr. Amadeus Arkham, the psychiatrist who founded the asylum. This story is told from journal excerpts discovered hidden in the hospital. They are the handwritten entries detailing his painful childhood, the difficulties of his profession in his adult life, and the tragic misfortune of his family. Unfortunately, these traumatic experiences shape him a dark way.<br><br>This was a dark and very psychological story. The artwork did a great job at highlighting the storyline and was a major part of the overall concept. I would definitely recommend this to any Batman fan and Joker fan. Thanks!</span>

<div id="review_251546814" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/251546814" />
    <a title="Julian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6195707-julian"><img alt="Julian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316857365p2/6195707.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/251546814?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julian" href="/user/show/6195707-julian">Julian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6195707-julian?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer251546814" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6253449498458137005">A batman tale at its best, as it reaches unflinchingly deep into the recesses of the human psyche. While the comic may be accused by some as symptomatic of an attempt at at best, pop psychology, I think the authors have done a marvellous job in portraying the differences by which Batman and The Joker are negotiating what are in essence, very similar psychological conflicts.<br/>This is done on a backdrop literally seething with a brooding, menacing perceived threat of total disintegration, which was </span>
  <span id="freeText6253449498458137005" style="display:none">A batman tale at its best, as it reaches unflinchingly deep into the recesses of the human psyche. While the comic may be accused by some as symptomatic of an attempt at at best, pop psychology, I think the authors have done a marvellous job in portraying the differences by which Batman and The Joker are negotiating what are in essence, very similar psychological conflicts.<br />This is done on a backdrop literally seething with a brooding, menacing perceived threat of total disintegration, which was in fact embraced by another main character, that of Arkham himself. An analytically minded reader will appreciate how each of Batman's villains in fact, symbolically represent in avatar form each of his specifc fears. <br />These fears make him human; while also confirming that his mask etc in fact serve as a defensive character armour which keeps the underlying guilt, abandonment rage and fantasies of revenge both at bay. At the same time, the mask also allows for sublimation in his role as a 'dark knight'. <br />There are nice references to Freudian theories (a connecting theme here is the loss of mother-via murder and imagined/actual matricide- and its associated trauma, annihilation anxiety and subsequent efforts at psychological defence), his structural theory of the mind (illustrated concretely by the architecture of the Asylum itself) Jungian archetypes, an implicit idealizing identification exhibited by Dr Cavendish (enabled by the Asylum again functioning as a container of chaos AND an evocative object), and even the role of 'similarity; in magic as described by James George Frazier in 'The Golden Bough'. This is the way fairy tales should be told (well, especially for adults)! Super-heroes are no longer just an all pervasive, concretely 'good' force dressed in a pretty costume,partaking in a sterile and entirely logical world whereby 'evil' villains are routinely 'defeated'. <br />No, this is a more realistic (albeit gruesome at times) confrontation of life and its culturally suppressed opposites (or should I say, inseparable shadow): death, chaos and disintegration.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6253449498458137005" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1969499874" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1969499874?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Briar&#39;s Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Briar&#39;s Reviews" href="/user/show/32054036-briar-s-reviews">Briar&#39;s Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=art">art</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=comics-graphic-novels">comics-graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=crime-mystery-suspense">crime-mystery-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=superhero">superhero</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1969499874" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1849690378931716763">I love comic books, but this one didn't do it for me.<br/><br/>I didn't like the art style, even if it was quite beautiful. For me, this style of comic didn't do Batman justice. It seemed very messy to me, and it didn't let me focus. I think this art style could work well with other characters, but not one where I want to pay attention to detail. It just felt to fuzzy.<br/><br/>There's footnotes in this edition, which seems really weird to me. Why does a comic book need footnotes? Shouldn't you be able to get the p</span>
  <span id="freeText1849690378931716763" style="display:none">I love comic books, but this one didn't do it for me.<br /><br />I didn't like the art style, even if it was quite beautiful. For me, this style of comic didn't do Batman justice. It seemed very messy to me, and it didn't let me focus. I think this art style could work well with other characters, but not one where I want to pay attention to detail. It just felt to fuzzy.<br /><br />There's footnotes in this edition, which seems really weird to me. Why does a comic book need footnotes? Shouldn't you be able to get the point across within the story?<br /><br />At least there was a script at the end to understand what was going on. It just seemed really weird to me that I had no honest idea what was happening. It didn't seem like a Batman comic, more like a parody of a Batman comic. Having to go back and forth between the comic and the script also left me incredibly frustrated. I don't understand how this comic book was supposed to hit audiences.<br /><br />The idea of having the inmates takes over Arkham Asylum seems awesome and this could make for the best story, but this art style didn't do it justice. I could barely tell what characters were who, and I'm obsessed with Batman. I also didn't understand the haunted part of the plot. <br /><br />I get this book was supposed to be a psychological thriller/horror that was supposed to attract adult and mature audiences, but it just didn't feel that way to me. The allusions and references went over my head, and I felt like there could have been so much more added to make it flow better.<br /><br />Overall, this book was super frustrating for me. I wanted to love it (especially when I paid way to much to get my hands on this book) but I just couldn't. I had high expectations and it came short.<br /><br />Two out of five stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1849690378931716763" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9788869712630" href="/book/show/27832552-arkham-asylum">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13998557-andrew?shelf=comics">comics</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1593874053" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer226642515428531718">Ok. I've heard about this title and I know there is a videogame inspired by this comic, but I never seen nothing, before today. While I was out of home, I stopped to comic book store, searching some good comics and I bought this.<br/><br/>The story start with patients of Arkham Asylum, many of them caught by Batman, that have took possession the building. The Dark Night is forced to enter, giving himself for the hostages, putting himself in the hands of his enemies. I read many favorite comments about thi</span>
  <span id="freeText226642515428531718" style="display:none">Ok. I've heard about this title and I know there is a videogame inspired by this comic, but I never seen nothing, before today. While I was out of home, I stopped to comic book store, searching some good comics and I bought this.<br /><br />The story start with patients of Arkham Asylum, many of them caught by Batman, that have took possession the building. The Dark Night is forced to enter, giving himself for the hostages, putting himself in the hands of his enemies. I read many favorite comments about this story and the artwork, but I'm not so satisfied.<br /><br />In this adventure, Batman is involved to a psychological game and forced, by his archenemy Joker, to face his inner demons, his dark side. But this is only a part of the story. Another part, tells about Amadeus Arkham, the founder of the asylum, that intersects with the main story.<br />And even this analysis of Batman is weak, I would have expected more.<br />There are many reference to symbolism and magic, quotes from Alice in Wonderland and a gloomy atmosphere that remind some horror writers, like H. P. Lovecraft.<br />The artwork undoubtedly has a certain charm, but looks often confused, difficult to understand and distressing.<br /><br />The whole story is original, even though too complicated. Too many ideas mixed togheter, but with a strong influence of horror.</span>
  <a data-text-id="226642515428531718" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11984006013786581196">3.5 stars. Superb art by Dave McKean and a mostly good story by Grant Morrison (with flashes of brilliance) highlight this quality Batman graphic novel. The reason it doesn't rate higher overall is because there were a few "huh?" moments where the story was a bit hard to follow and I think the creators at times sacrificed story at the altar of atmosphere. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_3112134002" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Kosta Voukelatos" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/107917946-kosta-voukelatos"><img alt="Kosta Voukelatos" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580640394p2/107917946.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3112134002?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kosta Voukelatos" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kosta Voukelatos" href="/user/show/107917946-kosta-voukelatos">Kosta Voukelatos</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3112134002" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12464814961691996991">"Arkham is a Looking Glass"<br/>-this specific line encapsulated what I believed to be one of the key purposes of this graphic novel which was to use Arkham Asylum as a means of delving into the psyche of Batman and making the readers question whether Batman is any more sane than the inmates of the asylum. This was accomplished through the incorporation of many villains from Batman's rogue gallery with the most notable being the Joker and Two-Face. The Joker was drawn in such a way that he came acros</span>
  <span id="freeText12464814961691996991" style="display:none">"Arkham is a Looking Glass"<br />-this specific line encapsulated what I believed to be one of the key purposes of this graphic novel which was to use Arkham Asylum as a means of delving into the psyche of Batman and making the readers question whether Batman is any more sane than the inmates of the asylum. This was accomplished through the incorporation of many villains from Batman's rogue gallery with the most notable being the Joker and Two-Face. The Joker was drawn in such a way that he came across as more of a horrifying and malevolent force of nature rather than the evil clown that he is usually portrayed as. <br /><br />The schizophrenic artwork combined with the excellent writing of Grant Morrison led to one of the most unique readings experiences i have ever had whilst reading a graphic novel. Consequently i believe that this graphic novel is worthy of a 5 star rating due to its ability to convey a surreal horror experience.<br /><br />My only criticism was at times I found the dialogue of the Joker to be written in such a jarring font that i found it barely legible. However, I found this to only be a minor annoyance that didn't detract from the intricately pieced together plot as well as the fantastic imagery.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12464814961691996991" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2203851337693694213">I know that a lot of the modern Batman mythos has a lot to do with the whole evil outside vs. darkness within motif, but this is ridiculous. What a pretentious bunch of nonsense. And I've never gotten the attraction to Dave McKean's art. But then, I'm not a goth nerd.   <span id="freeText2203851337693694213" style="display:none">I know that a lot of the modern Batman mythos has a lot to do with the whole evil outside vs. darkness within motif, but this is ridiculous. What a pretentious bunch of nonsense. And I've never gotten the attraction to Dave McKean's art. But then, I'm not a goth nerd. When did we let the British take over our comic books anyway? Neil Gaiman and co. need to stop trying to turn our national comic book industry into their own personal Kafka-at-Hot Topic wet dream. Somebody had to say it.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1611146062" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1611146062" />
    <a title="leynes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45198798-leynes"><img alt="leynes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593512704p2/45198798.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1611146062?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="leynes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="leynes" href="/user/show/45198798-leynes">leynes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1611146062" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12885732095803080059"><i>Batman: Arkham Asylum</i> is a very controversial comic book. Many full-fledged fans of the Caped Crusader hate this tale for its pretentiousness and over-the-top art style. Many comic book newbies find it way too inaccessible and nearly incomprehensible. And artsy people, like myself, just love it to death. <blockquote>
  <b>Sometimes... sometimes I think the Asylum is a head. We're inside a huge head that dreams us all into being. Perhaps it's your head, Batman. Arkham is a looking glass... and we are you.</b>
</blockquote>This </span>
  <span id="freeText12885732095803080059" style="display:none"><i>Batman: Arkham Asylum</i> is a very controversial comic book. Many full-fledged fans of the Caped Crusader hate this tale for its pretentiousness and over-the-top art style. Many comic book newbies find it way too inaccessible and nearly incomprehensible. And artsy people, like myself, just love it to death. <blockquote>
  <b>Sometimes... sometimes I think the Asylum is a head. We're inside a huge head that dreams us all into being. Perhaps it's your head, Batman. Arkham is a looking glass... and we are you.</b>
</blockquote>This is definitely not your typical Batman story. Bruce acts quite out of character for the most part. Usually, his main goal is to save innocent lives and make sure that everyone is unhurt in the given situation, whereas in <i>Batman: Arkham Asylum</i> he seems to be quite preoccupied with himself and his psyche, disregarding the fact that the Joker is threatening people left and right. On top of that, McKean's art style is something that you'll never see in comic books. He doesn't care for the conventions of the genre. I was first exposed to McKean when he did some of the cover art for Gaiman's <i>Sandman</i> and I fell in love with him right then. His art style is eery, hauntingly atmospheric and very diverse. He doesn't settle for one style, he is able to perfect many different facets, sometimes working with (what seem to be) almost life-like pictures and more often than not going for more of an obscure route. <br /><br /><i>Batman: Arkham Asylum</i> tells the story of how Batman is lured into the asylum for the criminally insane on April Fool's Day. The Joker has orchestrated a chain of events that is suppose to make Bruce face his own madness and his inner demons, specifically the death of his parents and how he became the Bat (we all know and love). Once trapped in the asylum, he inhales a drug that makes him hallucinate and nearly turn mad. Whilst running aimlessly through the place, Bruce encounters all of Gotham's criminals – all the psychopaths, sociopaths and poor souls we have come to know and love. <blockquote>
  <b>And I’m afraid that when I walk through those asylum gates... when I walk into Arkham and the doors close behind me... it’ll be just like coming home.</b>
</blockquote>Bruce faces Clayface who desperately wants to touch him and infest him with his disease. He is able to flee from the Mad Hatter and his weird paroles. He encounters Harvey Dent, now Two-Face, who is unable to make a decision without consulting his coin (...or a dice, or a pack of cards). He hears the Scarecrow shamble through Arkham's halls. And on top of that, the Joker who forces him to face it all. It is enough to even turn the Caped Crusader mad. <br /><br />Interwoven into Batman's narrative, is the backstory to Amadeus Arkham, the man who founded the asylum way back in the 1920s. We learn how he lost his mother, his wife and his daughter, and how that was enough to turn him mad. The parallels to Bruce's life are clear. <blockquote>
  <b>Oh, yes! Fill the churches with dirty thoughts! Introduce honesty to the White House! Write letters in dead languages to people you've never met! Paint filthy words on the foreheads of children! Burn your credit cards and wear high heels! Asylum doors stand open! Fill the suburbs with murder and rape! Divine madness! Let there be ecstasy, ecstasy in the streets! Laugh and the world laughs with you!</b>
</blockquote>Additionally to McKean's impeccable art style, I absolutely loved Morrison's writing. I can definitely understand why some might find it pretentious (see: “Einstein was wrong! I'M the speed of light CRACKING through shivery rainbows and GOD the sky whirls and withers like a melting RAINBOW!”) but in my humble opinion, he struck the right cord. I was creeped out by Bruce's fear. I was entertained by the Joker's madness. I loved the plot twist and the reveal about Harvey at the end. I like how the backstory to the asylum functioned as a parable to what was happening in the asylum today. <br /><br />Overall, I am absolutely satisfied with <i>Batman: Arkham Asylum</i> and would recommend it to people who are looking for something special and more unusual. The only negative thing I have to point out is the lettering for the Joker, his dialogue was incredibly hard to decipher, and that became a pain in the ass real quick. Apart from that, I absolutely adored this!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12885732095803080059" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3026335994" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3026335994" />
    <a title="Sud666" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36890366-sud666"><img alt="Sud666" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1418437112p2/36890366.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3026335994?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sud666" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sud666" href="/user/show/36890366-sud666">Sud666</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781401251246" href="/book/show/21556020-batman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36890366-sud666?shelf=comics">comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3026335994" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2144110878680762884">A serious house on serious earth it is,<br/>In whose blent air all our compulsions meet,<br/>Are recognised, and robed as destinies.<br/>And that much never can be obsolete,<br/>Since someone will forever be surprising<br/>A hunger in himself to be more serious,<br/>And gravitating with it to this ground,<br/>Which, he once heard, was proper to grow wise in,<br/>If only that so many dead lie round.<br/><br/>-Philiph Larkin "Church Going"<br/><br/>In 1989, Grant Morrison took a great deal of LSD and smoked a lot of weed and created one of the oddest, dist</span>
  <span id="freeText2144110878680762884" style="display:none">A serious house on serious earth it is,<br />In whose blent air all our compulsions meet,<br />Are recognised, and robed as destinies.<br />And that much never can be obsolete,<br />Since someone will forever be surprising<br />A hunger in himself to be more serious,<br />And gravitating with it to this ground,<br />Which, he once heard, was proper to grow wise in,<br />If only that so many dead lie round.<br /><br />-Philiph Larkin "Church Going"<br /><br />In 1989, Grant Morrison took a great deal of LSD and smoked a lot of weed and created one of the oddest, disturbing, bizarre and utterly brilliant graphic novels. Written in a time when the concept of a graphic novel would have been deemed as an oxymoron, "Batman: Arkham Asylum: A Serious House on Serious Earth" put paid to such calumny. <br /><br />GM decided to tell a Batman story focusing on the psychological pressures faced not only by Batman but by his various enemies as well. It is also a look into the mind of Dr. Amadeus Arkham, the founder of the Asylum.<br /><br />This controversial and odd graphic novel has set the stage for the current Batman world. This is the definitive "version" of Arkham and influenced the way in which the Asylum is portrayed even in the current timeline. In fact the video game, Arkham Asylum, was loosely based on this very concept.<br /><br />The gist of the plot? The inmates of Arkham have rioted and taken control, they ask for only one thing-Batman. Batman enters the asylum, confronts his nemesis in the form of Joker, fights some villains and learns a lot about himself and Dr. Arkham.<br /><br />The dialogue is odd but deep. The visuals? It's a LSD trip on pages. The story could be said to be influenced by such diverse subjects inspired by Lewis Carroll, quantum physics, Jung, and Crowley. The art? GM said that he was influenced by surrealism: " Eastern European creepiness, Cocteau, Artaud, Švankmajer, the Brothers Quay, etc. The intention was to create something that was more like a piece of music or an experimental film than a typical adventure comic book. "<br /><br />The end result is anything but a "typical" comic book. Some people hate this graphic novel, while others love it. I am somewhere in the middle leaning towards "this is an amazing piece of imaginative art". Sometimes the visuals can be offputting and confuse the story, but since this is a story about the insane inmates of the Asylum- the motif fits.<br /><br />GM said that " The construction of the story was influenced by the architecture of a house — the past and the tale of Amadeus Arkham forms the basement levels. Secret passages connect ideas and segments of the book. There are upper stories of unfolding symbol and metaphor. We were also referencing sacred geometry, and the plan of the Arkham House was based on the Glastonbury Abbey and Chartres Cathedral. The journey through the book is like moving through the floors of the house itself. The house and the head are one."<br /><br />The 25th Anniversary edition has a bunch of extra information, interviews with GM and additional information. As such it was a great addition to my collection. If you've never read this graphic novel, do yourself a favor and try it. I can not guarantee you will like it, but I promise it will be like nothing you've ever read or seen before.<br /><br />Journey into the madness that is Arkham Asylum.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2144110878680762884" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_621113668" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/621113668" />
    <a title="Brandon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3214163-brandon"><img alt="Brandon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603283104p2/3214163.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/621113668?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brandon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brandon" href="/user/show/3214163-brandon">Brandon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3214163-brandon?shelf=comix">comix</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3214163-brandon?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3214163-brandon?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3214163-brandon?shelf=disappointments">disappointments</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer621113668" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6034756890670642039">Batman is alerted that the inmates of Arkham Asylum have taken over the premises. If this isn't dangerous enough, they're threatening to murder everyone in the facility unless Batman agrees to a face to face meeting.<br/><br/>I understand that a lot of people can appreciate the style in which both Morrison and McKean approached Batman, however this just wasn't for me. Maybe I like my stuff a little more.. focused? I have no idea if that's the right word. I feel like I'm almost speaking a form of blasphemy</span>
  <span id="freeText6034756890670642039" style="display:none">Batman is alerted that the inmates of Arkham Asylum have taken over the premises. If this isn't dangerous enough, they're threatening to murder everyone in the facility unless Batman agrees to a face to face meeting.<br /><br />I understand that a lot of people can appreciate the style in which both Morrison and McKean approached Batman, however this just wasn't for me. Maybe I like my stuff a little more.. focused? I have no idea if that's the right word. I feel like I'm almost speaking a form of blasphemy here by not loving this book.<br /><br />That being said, I certainly do not want to take anything away from Dave McKean - the guy is crazy talented. I just question whether or not this really works within the constraints of a comic book. I thought the scenes were unfocused and hard for me as a reader to follow. I guess when it came down to it, I had a lot of trouble grasping exactly what I was looking at. I'll give McKean credit for trying something outside-the-box but I feel like the whole presentation was lost on me. Also, a lot of the dialogue contained some strange choices. In particular, Morrison having Batman scream, "Jesus!" felt weird and awkward to me.<br /><br />Before you jump down my throat, it wasn't all bad. I'll say that I liked the idea of giving each character their own specific font when they spoke. Joker's sharp words cutting through the atmosphere gave his madness that extra intensity. Apparently, this is something that is considered an industry standard today but it all began with Gaspar Saladino's superb lettering.<br /><br />I guess I appreciate what was attempted but I'm not sure I could bring myself to read it again or who exactly I'd recommend this to.<br /><br />Cross Posted @ <a href="http://everyreadthing.wordpress.com/2013/05/24/arkham-asylum/" rel="nofollow noopener">Every Read Thing</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6034756890670642039" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1021747018" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1021747018" />
    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1021747018?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">no one</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=2014-challenge-factory-challenge">2014-challenge-factory-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=dangerous-hero-challenge-2014">dangerous-hero-challenge-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=2014-graphic-novel-reading-challeng">2014-graphic-novel-reading-challeng</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=library-checkout">library-checkout</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=2014-cover-to-cover-challenge">2014-cover-to-cover-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=graphic-novel-comic-book">graphic-novel-comic-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1021747018" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17974920225253169832">My dislike of this book borders on violent. I realize what the author and artist were going for, and I appreciate the foreward and even the screenplay with commentary. I admit I gave up on reading the whole screenplay because I was tired and wasn't feeling well, and felt my time was better spent moving on. However, even gaining insight into their thought processes didn't make me like this book any more.<br/><br/>I am an artist, and I love art. However, I am not a fan of art becoming so all-consuming that </span>
  <span id="freeText17974920225253169832" style="display:none">My dislike of this book borders on violent. I realize what the author and artist were going for, and I appreciate the foreward and even the screenplay with commentary. I admit I gave up on reading the whole screenplay because I was tired and wasn't feeling well, and felt my time was better spent moving on. However, even gaining insight into their thought processes didn't make me like this book any more.<br /><br />I am an artist, and I love art. However, I am not a fan of art becoming so all-consuming that it loses meaning to the average person. In other words, I like my art to be accessible. This book wasn't. It was full of social commentary, allusions, and symbolism, which can be good in therapeutic doses. But even medicine can be toxic when overdosed. I think that is a good way to describe my feelings for this book. It was toxic with the statements of the creators, and it killed the overall book.<br /><br />Some of my individual issues:<br /><br />*The lettering was nearly incomprehensible, especially the Joker's words and thoughts. I am very near-sighted, and I am getting where small print gives me fits. The Joker's print was in red, and the font was very scribbly. Everyone knows that the Joker is bat*&amp;$# crazy. I understand where Morrison and McKean were trying to go here showing how chaotic his mind was, but it fell on deaf ears since I had trouble reading the lettering. Also obscure symbology dispersed through this volume makes no sense to me. Another place where it falls flat, since it seems to have no purpose in this volume.<br /><br />*Batman was played as anal-retentive to the extreme. I'm not sure I appreciated this. Admittedly, Batman does have some psychological issues he's working through--he's a control freak and is incredibly uptight and is at times intolerant. I think his portrayal in this book was unpalatable, showing him as pathologically damaged. That isn't the Batman I know and deeply respect.<br /><br />*The storyline about Arkham, the founder of the Asylum was okay. Although I didn't like what happened to his family, and the view of his relationship with his mother was way too Freudian for my tastes.<br /><br />*The artwork is nebulous and difficult to cipher and track over the panels. I would almost call it abstract. Does that work for a comic book medium? I'm going to say no. If I can't follow it, it has failed to convey meaning to me.<br /><br />I know that this is a very highly praised and critically-acclaimed book, but I'm not a fan of it. Art is meaning to me. While art is highly subjective, the viewer has to have a lens through which to take in and process the work. In this book, the lens is cloudy and muddled. There is no avenue to look deeper.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17974920225253169832" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_204182598" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/204182598" />
    <a title="Sesana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana"><img alt="Sesana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413088169p2/5172893.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/204182598?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sesana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sesana" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana">Sesana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=superhumans">superhumans</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer204182598" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2182329978021712304">I admit, I picked this up for a re-read after playing Arkham Asylum. Fantastic game, by the way, well-written, with great action and incredible voice acting. But this is not about that game, about which I could rave for hours.<br/><br/>I remember loving this graphic novel when I first read it, but reading it again I can't exactly remember why. It's still well-written, and the Arkham backstory is interesting enough that it's apparently been kept. But pretty much everybody that shows up feels out of charact</span>
  <span id="freeText2182329978021712304" style="display:none">I admit, I picked this up for a re-read after playing Arkham Asylum. Fantastic game, by the way, well-written, with great action and incredible voice acting. But this is not about that game, about which I could rave for hours.<br /><br />I remember loving this graphic novel when I first read it, but reading it again I can't exactly remember why. It's still well-written, and the Arkham backstory is interesting enough that it's apparently been kept. But pretty much everybody that shows up feels out of character, sometimes slightly and sometimes... more than slightly. Batman in particular is way more psychologically unstable than normal (and he's not exactly a paragon of sanity, let's be honest). Joker just felt slightly off in a way that's hard to put my finger on. <br /><br />The pacing is also slightly odd. There's a rushed feeling to the middle section, which really could have used a few more pages. And because this was initially released as a trade, it probably could have had them. The basic plot itself (the Batman villains take over Arkham and invite Batman inside) is really a good idea. Obviously, since it was used as the basic plot for the game. But how often is the video game adaptation better than the original? In particular, the game has much better pacing, actual goals for Batman to accomplish, and a distinct and chillingly good plot from the Joker. The plot in the book is much more vague.<br /><br />The art is... well, it's what Dave McKean was doing at the time. I like McKean's work, a lot, and I think he's frequently brilliant, but it's very much an acquired taste. A lot of people are going to hate it intensely. Does it fit in the world of Batman? Not normally. In this book? Well, that's a matter of opinion. I think it suits the storyline, barely, but I probably would have rather had something a bit more... conventional. At least in certain spots, the art can actually detract from the story. <br /><br />A good idea that could have been better. Just ask the makers of the video game.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2182329978021712304" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
